   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Angola</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the modern country since 1992. For the former country from 1975 to 1992, see <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Angola" title="People's Republic of Angola">People's Republic of Angola</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Angola_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Angola (disambiguation)">Angola (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country on the west coast of Southern Africa
      </div>

         <td>negligible</td>

      <p><b>Angola</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Angola-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/En-Angola-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Angola-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <span style="font-size:85%;">Portuguese:&nbsp;</span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ɐ̃ˈɡɔlɐ]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Angola</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">República de Angola</i>), is a country in the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>. It is the second largest <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">lusophone</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_entities_where_Portuguese_is_an_official_language" title="List of territorial entities where Portuguese is an official language">Portuguese-speaking</a>) country in both total area and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">population</a> (behind <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>), and it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_area" title="List of African countries by area">seventh-largest</a> country in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the south, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west. Angola has an <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a> province, the province of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda</a> that borders the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> and the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>. </p>
      <p>Angola has been inhabited since the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic Age</a>. Its formation as a nation state originates from <a href="/wiki/European_exploration_of_Africa" title="European exploration of Africa">Portuguese colonisation</a>, which initially began with coastal settlements and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> founded in the 16th century. In the 19th century, European settlers gradually began to establish themselves in the interior. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese colony</a> that became Angola did not have its present borders until the early 20th century, owing to resistance by native groups such as the Cuamato, the <a href="/wiki/Oukwanyama" title="Oukwanyama">Kwanyama</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a>. </p>
      <p>After a protracted <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">anti-colonial struggle</a>, Angola achieved independence in 1975 as a <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist–Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Angola" title="People's Republic of Angola">one-party republic</a>. The country descended into a devastating <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war</a> the same year, between the ruling <a href="/wiki/MPLA" title="MPLA">People's Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> (MPLA), backed by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and the insurgent anti-communist <a href="/wiki/UNITA" title="UNITA">National Union for the Total Independence of Angola</a> (UNITA), supported by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. Following the end of the war in 2002, Angola emerged as a relatively stable <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">constitutional republic</a>. </p>
      <p>Angola has vast <a href="/wiki/Mineral_resource_estimation" title="Mineral resource estimation">mineral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">petroleum reserves</a>, and its economy is among the fastest-growing in the world, especially since the end of the civil war. However, economic growth is highly uneven, with most of the nation's <a href="/wiki/Distribution_of_wealth#Wealth_concentration" title="Distribution of wealth">wealth concentrated</a> in a disproportionately small sector of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a> remains low for most Angolans; <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is among the lowest in the world, while <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> is among the highest.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Angola is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>. Its population of 25.8 million is multicultural and multiethnic. Angolan culture reflects centuries of Portuguese rule, namely the predominance of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, intermingled with a variety of indigenous customs and traditions. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name <i>Angola</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> colonial name <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text"><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Reino de Angola</a></i> ('Kingdom of Angola'), which appeared as early as <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Dias_de_Novais" title="Paulo Dias de Novais">Paulo Dias de Novais</a>'s 1571 charter.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponym</a> was derived by the Portuguese from the title <i lang="kmb" title="Kimbundu-language text"><a href="/wiki/List_of_Ngolas_of_Ndongo" title="List of Ngolas of Ndongo">ngola</a></i> held by the kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Ndongo</a>. Ndongo in the <a href="/wiki/Highland" title="Highland">highlands</a>, between the <a href="/wiki/Cuanza_River" title="Cuanza River">Kwanza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucala_River" title="Lucala River">Lucala Rivers</a>, was nominally a possession of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>, but was seeking greater independence in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Angola" title="History of Angola">History of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_migrations_and_political_units">Early migrations and political units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early migrations and political units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg/170px-Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg/255px-Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg/340px-Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="459" data-file-height="760"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Jean_Roy_de_Congo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_I_of_Kongo" title="João I of Kongo">King João I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manikongo" title="Manikongo">Manikongo</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Modern Angola was populated predominantly by <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> <a href="/wiki/Khoi" class="mw-redirect" title="Khoi">Khoi</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a> prior to the first <a href="/wiki/Bantu_migration" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu migration">Bantu migrations</a>. The Khoi and San peoples were neither <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralists</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Cultivator" title="Cultivator">cultivators</a>, but rather <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Henderson_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson-11">[11]</a></sup> They were displaced by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> arriving from the north in the first millennium BC, most of whom likely originated in what is today northwestern <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller1-12">[12]</a></sup> Bantu speakers introduced the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a>, as well as large cattle herds, to Angola's central highlands and the Luanda plain. </p>
      <p>A number of political entities were established; the best-known of these was the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Kongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of the Kongo">Kingdom of the Kongo</a>, based in Angola, which extended northward to what is now the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>. It established <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> with other city-states and civilisations up and down the coast of southwestern and western Africa and even with <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">Great Zimbabwe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mutapa_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutapa Empire">Mutapa Empire</a>, although it engaged in little or no transoceanic trade.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Story_of_Africa_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Story_of_Africa-13">[13]</a></sup> To its south lay the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Kingdom of Ndongo</a>, from which the area of the later Portuguese colony was sometimes known as <i>Dongo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_colonization">Portuguese colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Portuguese colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_Angola" title="Colonial history of Angola">Colonial history of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg/170px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg/255px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg/340px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="352" data-file-height="502"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Kingdom_of_Kongo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Coat of arms granted to King <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Kongo" title="Afonso I of Kongo">Afonso I of Kongo</a> by King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo Cão">Diogo Cão</a> reached the area in 1484.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-14">[14]</a></sup> The previous year, the Portuguese had established relations with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a>, which stretched at the time from modern <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/Kwanza_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwanza River">Kwanza River</a> in the south. The Portuguese established their primary early trading post at <a href="/wiki/Soyo" title="Soyo">Soyo</a>, which is now the northernmost city in Angola apart from the <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda</a> <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a>. <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Dias_de_Novais" title="Paulo Dias de Novais">Paulo Dias de Novais</a> founded São Paulo de Loanda (<a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>) in 1575 with a hundred families of settlers and four hundred soldiers. <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a> was fortified in 1587 and became a township in 1617. </p>
      <p>The Portuguese established several other settlements, forts and trading posts along the Angolan coast, principally trading in <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Angola" title="Slavery in Angola">Angolan slaves</a> for <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantations in the American South">plantations</a>. Local slave dealers provided a large number of slaves for the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Fleisch_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fleisch-15">[15]</a></sup> usually in exchange for manufactured goods from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> continued until after <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Brazil's</a> <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence</a> in the 1820s.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/220px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/330px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/440px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png 2x" data-file-width="1438" data-file-height="953"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nzinga_of_Ndongo_and_Matamba" title="Nzinga of Ndongo and Matamba">Queen Ana de Sousa of Ndongo</a> meeting with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, 1657
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg/220px-Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="77" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg/330px-Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg/440px-Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3219" data-file-height="1131"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_de_S%C3%A3o_Paulo_da_Assump%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Loanda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Depiction of <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> from 1755
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite Portugal's territorial claims in Angola, its control over much of the country's vast interior was minimal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-14">[14]</a></sup> In the 16th century Portugal gained control of the coast through a series of treaties and wars. Life for European colonists was difficult and progress slow. <a href="/wiki/John_Iliffe_(historian)" title="John Iliffe (historian)">John Iliffe</a> notes that "Portuguese records of Angola from the 16th century show that a great <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> occurred on average every seventy years; accompanied by epidemic disease, it might kill one-third or one-half of the population, destroying the demographic growth of a generation and forcing colonists back into the river valleys".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Loango-Angola" title="Dutch Loango-Angola">occupied</a> the principal settlement of Luanda in 1641, using alliances with local peoples to carry out attacks against Portuguese holdings elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-18">[18]</a></sup> A fleet under <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_S%C3%A1" title="Salvador de Sá">Salvador de Sá</a> retook Luanda in 1648; reconquest of the rest of the territory was completed by 1650. New treaties with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a> were signed in 1649; others with <a href="/wiki/Nzinga_of_Ndongo_and_Matamba" title="Nzinga of Ndongo and Matamba">Njinga</a>'s Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Matamba" class="mw-redirect" title="Matamba">Matamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ndongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Ndongo">Ndongo</a> followed in 1656. The conquest of <a href="/wiki/Pungo_Andongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Pungo Andongo">Pungo Andongo</a> in 1671 was the last major Portuguese expansion from Luanda, as attempts to invade Kongo in 1670 and Matamba in 1681 failed. Colonial outposts also expanded inward from Benguela, but until the late 19th century the inroads from Luanda and Benguela were very limited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-14">[14]</a></sup> Hamstrung by a series of political upheavals in the early 1800s, Portugal was slow to mount a large scale annexation of Angolan territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-18">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cadornega.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cadornega.jpg/170px-Cadornega.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cadornega.jpg/255px-Cadornega.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Cadornega.jpg/340px-Cadornega.jpg 2x" data-file-width="642" data-file-height="975"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cadornega.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>History of Angola</i>; written in Luanda in 1680.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> was abolished in Angola in 1836, and in 1854 the colonial government freed all its existing slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-18">[18]</a></sup> Four years later, a more progressive administration appointed by Lisbon abolished <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> altogether. However, these decrees remained largely unenforceable, and the Portuguese depended on assistance from the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> to enforce their ban on the slave trade.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-18">[18]</a></sup> This coincided with a series of renewed military expeditions into the bush. </p>
      <p>By the mid-nineteenth century Portugal had established its dominion as far east as the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and as far south as <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%A7%C3%A2medes" title="Moçâmedes">Mossâmedes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbook_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-18">[18]</a></sup> Until the late 1880s, Lisbon entertained proposals to link Angola with its <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> but was blocked by British and Belgian opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-Corrado_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado-20">[20]</a></sup> In this period, the Portuguese came up against different forms of armed resistance from various peoples in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> in 1884–1885 set the colony's borders, delineating the boundaries of Portuguese claims in Angola,<sup id="cite_ref-Corrado_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado-20">[20]</a></sup> although many details were unresolved until the 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Trade between Portugal and its African territories rapidly increased as a result of protective <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a>, leading to increased development, and a wave of new Portuguese immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-Corrado_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angolan_independence">Angolan independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Angolan independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">Angolan War of Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Luanda,desfilemilitar_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Luanda%2Cdesfilemilitar_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Luanda%2Cdesfilemilitar_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Luanda%2Cdesfilemilitar_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Luanda%2Cdesfilemilitar_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Luanda%2Cdesfilemilitar_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Luanda%2Cdesfilemilitar_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="337"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Luanda,desfilemilitar_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Armed_Forces" title="Portuguese Armed Forces">Portuguese Armed Forces</a> marching in Luanda during the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial Wars</a> (1961-74).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Under colonial law, black Angolans were forbidden from forming political parties or labour unions.<sup id="cite_ref-Okoth_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okoth-23">[23]</a></sup> The first nationalist movements did not take root until after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, spearheaded by a largely Westernised, Portuguese-speaking urban class which included many <a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mestiço">mestiços</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dowden_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dowden-24">[24]</a></sup> During the early 1960s they were joined by other associations stemming from <i>ad hoc</i> labour activism in the rural workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-Okoth_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okoth-23">[23]</a></sup> Portugal's refusal to address increasing Angolan demands for <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a> provoked an armed conflict which erupted in 1961 with the <a href="/wiki/Baixa_de_Cassanje_revolt" title="Baixa de Cassanje revolt">Baixa de Cassanje revolt</a> and gradually evolved into a protracted <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">war of independence</a> that persisted for the next twelve years.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornwell_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-25">[25]</a></sup> Throughout the conflict, three militant nationalist movements with their own partisan guerrilla wings emerged from the fighting between the Portuguese government and local forces, supported to varying degrees by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Communist_Party" title="Portuguese Communist Party">Portuguese Communist Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dowden_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dowden-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stockwell_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stockwell-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/FNLA" class="mw-redirect" title="FNLA">National Front for the Liberation of Angola</a></i> (FNLA) recruited from <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a> refugees in <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hanlon_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanlon-27">[27]</a></sup> Benefiting from particularly favourable political circumstances in <a href="/wiki/Kinshasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Kinshasha">Léopoldville</a>, and especially from a common border with Zaire, Angolan political exiles were able to build up a power base among a large expatriate community from related families, clans, and traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Chabal_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-28">[28]</a></sup> People on both sides of the border spoke mutually intelligible dialects and enjoyed shared ties to the historical Kingdom of Kongo.<sup id="cite_ref-Chabal_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-28">[28]</a></sup> Though as foreigners skilled Angolans could not take advantage of <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a>'s state employment programme, some found work as middlemen for the absentee owners of various lucrative private ventures. The migrants eventually formed the FNLA with the intention of making a bid for political power upon their envisaged return to Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-Chabal_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FNLA1973.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/FNLA1973.jpg/220px-FNLA1973.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/FNLA1973.jpg/330px-FNLA1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/FNLA1973.jpg/440px-FNLA1973.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2525" data-file-height="2529"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FNLA1973.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_of_Angola" title="National Liberation Front of Angola">National Liberation Front of Angola</a> training in 1973.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A largely <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> guerrilla initiative against the Portuguese in central Angola from 1966 was spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Savimbi" title="Jonas Savimbi">Jonas Savimbi</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/UNITA" title="UNITA">National Union for the Total Independence of Angola</a></i> (UNITA).<sup id="cite_ref-Hanlon_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanlon-27">[27]</a></sup> It remained handicapped by its geographic remoteness from friendly borders, the ethnic fragmentation of the Ovimbundu, and the isolation of peasants on European plantations where they had little opportunity to mobilise.<sup id="cite_ref-Chabal_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the late 1950s, the rise of the Marxist–Leninist <i><a href="/wiki/MPLA" title="MPLA">Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a></i> (MPLA) in the east and Dembos hills north of Luanda came to hold special significance. Formed as a coalition resistance movement by the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Communist_Party" title="Angolan Communist Party">Angolan Communist Party</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Cornwell_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-25">[25]</a></sup> the organisation's leadership remained predominantly <a href="/wiki/Ambundu" title="Ambundu">Ambundu</a> and courted public sector workers in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hanlon_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanlon-27">[27]</a></sup> Although both the MPLA and its rivals accepted material assistance from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> or the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, the former harboured strong anti-imperialist views and was openly critical of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and its support for Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-Stockwell_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stockwell-26">[26]</a></sup> This allowed it to win important ground on the diplomatic front, soliciting support from nonaligned governments in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornwell_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The MPLA attempted to move its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> to Léopoldville in October 1961, renewing efforts to create a common front with the FNLA, then known as the <i>Union of Angolan Peoples</i> (UPA) and its leader <a href="/wiki/Holden_Roberto" title="Holden Roberto">Holden Roberto</a>. Roberto turned down the offer.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornwell_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-25">[25]</a></sup> When the MPLA first attempted to insert its own insurgents into Angola, the cadres were ambushed and annihilated by UPA partisans on Roberto's orders—setting a precedent for the bitter factional strife which would later ignite the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornwell_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angolan_Civil_war">Angolan Civil war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Angolan Civil war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_MPLA,_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_(r),_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/President_MPLA%2C_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_%28r%29%2C_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-President_MPLA%2C_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_%28r%29%2C_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/President_MPLA%2C_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_%28r%29%2C_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-President_MPLA%2C_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_%28r%29%2C_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/President_MPLA%2C_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_%28r%29%2C_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-President_MPLA%2C_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_%28r%29%2C_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1569" data-file-height="2013"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_MPLA,_heer_Neto_door_Den_Uyl_ontvangen_premier_Den_Uyl_en_A_Neto_(r),_Bestanddeelnr_927-8518_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto" title="Agostinho Neto">Agostinho Neto</a>, first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Angola" title="President of Angola">President of Angola</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Throughout the war of independence, the three rival nationalist movements were severely hampered by political and military factionalism, as well as their inability to unite guerrilla efforts against the Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> Between 1961 and 1975 the MPLA, UNITA, and the FNLA competed for influence in the Angolan population and the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> became especially sympathetic towards the MPLA and supplied that party with arms, ammunition, funding, and training.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> They also backed UNITA militants until it became clear that the latter was at irreconcilable odds with the MPLA.<sup id="cite_ref-Revolution_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revolution-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The collapse of Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> government following the 1974 <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> suspended all Portuguese military activity in Africa and the brokering of a ceasefire pending negotiations for Angolan independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> Encouraged by the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a>, Holden Roberto, Jonas Savimbi, and MPLA chairman <a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto" title="Agostinho Neto">Agostinho Neto</a> met in <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> in early January 1975 and agreed to form a coalition government.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> This was ratified by the <a href="/wiki/Alvor_Agreement" title="Alvor Agreement">Alvor Agreement</a> later that month, which called for general elections and set the country's independence date for 11 November 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> All three factions, however, followed up on the ceasefire by taking advantage of the gradual Portuguese withdrawal to seize various strategic positions, acquire more arms, and enlarge their militant forces.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> The rapid influx of weapons from numerous external sources, especially the Soviet Union and the United States, as well as the escalation of tensions between the nationalist parties, fueled a new outbreak of hostilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> With tacit American and Zairean support the FNLA began massing large numbers of troops in northern Angola in an attempt to gain military superiority.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the MPLA began securing control of Luanda, a traditional Ambundu stronghold.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> Sporadic violence broke out in Luanda over the next few months after the FNLA attacked MPLA forces in March 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> The fighting intensified with street clashes in April and May, and UNITA became involved after over two hundred of its members were massacred by an MPLA contingent that June.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> An upswing in Soviet arms shipments to the MPLA influenced a decision by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> to likewise provide substantial covert aid to the FNLA and UNITA.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanneman_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png/240px-South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png" decoding="async" width="240" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png/360px-South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png/480px-South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="926" data-file-height="572"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:South_Africa_Border_War_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maximum extent of <a href="/wiki/UNITA" title="UNITA">UNITA</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_African_Border_War" title="South African Border War">South African</a> operations in Angola and Zambia during the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In August 1975, the MPLA requested direct assistance from the Soviet Union in the form of ground troops.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanneman_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-32">[32]</a></sup> The Soviets declined, offering to send advisers but no troops; however, Cuba was more forthcoming and in late September dispatched nearly five hundred combat personnel to Angola, along with sophisticated weaponry and supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-Revolution_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Revolution-30">[30]</a></sup> By independence there were over a thousand Cuban soldiers in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanneman_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-32">[32]</a></sup> They were kept supplied by a massive <a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Angola_airbridge" title="Cuba–Angola airbridge">airbridge</a> carried out with Soviet aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanneman_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-32">[32]</a></sup> The persistent buildup of Cuban and Soviet military aid allowed the MPLA to drive its opponents from Luanda and blunt an abortive intervention by Zairean and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> troops, which had deployed in a belated attempt to assist the FNLA and UNITA.<sup id="cite_ref-Weigert_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-31">[31]</a></sup> The FNLA was largely annihilated, although UNITA managed to withdraw its civil officials and militia from Luanda and seek sanctuary in the southern provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-29">[29]</a></sup> From there, Savimbi continued to mount a determined insurgent campaign against the MPLA.<sup id="cite_ref-Vanneman_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/210px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" decoding="async" width="210" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/315px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/420px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG 2x" data-file-width="616" data-file-height="579"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cuban tank in Luanda during the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_intervention_in_Angola" title="Cuban intervention in Angola">Cuban intervention in Angola</a>, 1976
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Between 1975 and 1991, the MPLA implemented an economic and political system based on the principles of <a href="/wiki/Scientific_socialism" title="Scientific socialism">scientific socialism</a>, incorporating <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">central planning</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist–Leninist">Marxist–Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Arming_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-33">[33]</a></sup> It embarked on an ambitious programme of <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalisation</a>, and the domestic private sector was essentially abolished.<sup id="cite_ref-Arming_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-33">[33]</a></sup> Privately owned enterprises were nationalised and incorporated into a single umbrella of state-owned enterprises known as <i>Unidades Economicas Estatais</i> (UEE).<sup id="cite_ref-Arming_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-33">[33]</a></sup> Under the MPLA, Angola experienced a significant degree of modern <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Arming_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-33">[33]</a></sup> However, corruption and graft also increased and public resources were either allocated inefficiently or simply embezzled by officials for personal enrichment.<sup id="cite_ref-SSG1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SSG1-34">[34]</a></sup> The ruling party survived an attempted coup d'état by the <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoist</a>-oriented <a href="/wiki/Communist_Organization_of_Angola" title="Communist Organization of Angola">Communist Organisation of Angola</a> (OCA) in 1977, which was suppressed after a series of bloody political purges left thousands of OCA supporters dead.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker1-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The MPLA abandoned its former Marxist ideology at its third party congress in 1990, and declared <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a> to be its new platform.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker1_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker1-35">[35]</a></sup> Angola subsequently became a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>; restrictions on the market economy were also reduced in an attempt to draw foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-Tordoff1_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tordoff1-36">[36]</a></sup> By May 1991 it reached a peace agreement with UNITA, the <a href="/wiki/Bicesse_Accords" title="Bicesse Accords">Bicesse Accords</a>, which scheduled <a href="/wiki/Angolan_general_election,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Angolan general election, 1992">new general elections</a> for September 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-Tordoff1_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tordoff1-36">[36]</a></sup> When the MPLA secured a major electoral victory, UNITA objected to the results of both the presidential and legislative vote count and returned to war.<sup id="cite_ref-Tordoff1_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tordoff1-36">[36]</a></sup> Following the election, the <a href="/wiki/Halloween_massacre_(Angola)" title="Halloween massacre (Angola)">Halloween massacre</a> occurred from 30 October to 1 November, where MPLA forces killed thousands of UNITA supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/220px-Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/330px-Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/440px-Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Porto_de_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> is experiencing widespread urban renewal and redevelopment in the 21st century, backed largely by profits from oil &amp; diamond industries.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2000s_in_Angola" title="2000s in Angola">2000s in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 22 March 2002, Jonas Savimbi was killed in action against government troops. UNITA and the MPLA reached a cease-fire shortly afterwards. UNITA gave up its armed wing and assumed the role of a major opposition party. Although the political situation of the country began to stabilise, regular democratic processes did not prevail until the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Angola" title="Elections in Angola">elections in Angola</a> in 2008 and 2012 and the adoption of a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">constitution</a> in 2010, all of which strengthened the prevailing <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant-party system</a>. </p>
      <p>Angola has a serious humanitarian crisis; the result of the prolonged war, of the abundance of <a href="/wiki/Minefield" class="mw-redirect" title="Minefield">minefields</a>, of the continued political (and to a much lesser degree) military activities in favour of the independence of the <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a> (carried out in the context of the protracted <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_War" title="Cabinda War">Cabinda conflict</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">FLEC</a>), but most of all, by the depredation of the country's rich mineral resources by the régime.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While most of the internally displaced have now settled around the capital, in the so-called <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/musseque" class="extiw" title="wikt:musseque">musseques</a></i>, the general situation for Angolans remains desperate.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">Drought</a> in 2016 caused the worst food crisis in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a> in 25 years. Drought affected 1.4 million people across seven of Angola's 18 provinces. <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">Food prices</a> rose and acute <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> rates doubled, with more than 95,000 children affected. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos" title="José Eduardo dos Santos">José Eduardo dos Santos</a> stepped down as <a href="/wiki/President_of_Angola" title="President of Angola">President of Angola</a> after 38 years in 2017, being peacefully succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o" title="João Lourenço">João Lourenço</a>, Santos' chosen successor. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Angola" title="Geography of Angola">Geography of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Angola_Topography.png/170px-Angola_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Angola_Topography.png/255px-Angola_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Angola_Topography.png/340px-Angola_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="1318" data-file-height="1387"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topography of Angola.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">

          <div class="thumbcaption">

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 1,246,620&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (481,321&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Angola is the world's twenty-third largest country - comparable in size to Mali, or twice the size of France or of Texas. It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_south" title="4th parallel south">4°</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_south" title="18th parallel south">18°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_meridian_east" title="24th meridian east">24°E</a>. </p>
      <p>Angola borders <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the north-east and the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="South Atlantic Ocean">South Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west. </p>
      <p>The coastal <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a> in the north has borders with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the north and with the Democratic Republic of the Congo to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Angola's capital, <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, lies on the Atlantic coast in the northwest of the country. </p>
      <p>Angola had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.35/10, ranking it 23<sup>rd</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Angola">Climate of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Angola, although located in a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical zone">tropical zone</a>, has a climate uncharacteristic of this zone, due to the confluence of three factors: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>the cold <a href="/wiki/Benguela_Current" title="Benguela Current">Benguela Current</a> flowing along the southern part of the coast</li> 
       <li>the relief in the interior</li> 
       <li>the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Namib Desert">Namib Desert</a> in the southwest</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Angola's climate features two seasons: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>rainfall from November to April</li> 
       <li>drought, known as <i>Cacimbo</i>, from May to October, drier, as the name implies, and with lower temperatures</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>While the coastline has high rainfall rates, decreasing from north to south and from 800 millimetres (31 inches) to 50 millimetres (2.0 inches), with average annual temperatures above 23&nbsp;°C (73&nbsp;°F), one can divide the interior zone into three areas:<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>North, with high rainfall and high temperatures</li> 
       <li>Central Plateau, with a dry season and average temperatures of the order of 19&nbsp;°C</li> 
       <li>South, with very high thermal amplitudes due to the proximity of the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a> and the influence of masses of tropical air</li>
      </ul>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of March 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Angola is divided into <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Angola" title="Provinces of Angola">eighteen provinces</a> (<i>províncias</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of Angola">162 municipalities</a>. The municipalities are further divided into 559 communes (townships).<sup id="cite_ref-acd_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acd-47">[47]</a></sup> The provinces are: </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exclave_of_Cabinda">Exclave of Cabinda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Exclave of Cabinda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda Province</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_(19543179475)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_%2819543179475%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_%2819543179475%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_%2819543179475%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_%2819543179475%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_%2819543179475%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_%2819543179475%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="987" data-file-height="502"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Governo_Provincial_do_Namibe_(19543179475)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Namibe_Province" title="Namibe Province">Provincial Government of Namibe</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With an area of approximately 7,283 square kilometres (2,812&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), the Northern Angolan province of Cabinda is unusual in being separated from the rest of the country by a strip, some 60 kilometres (37&nbsp;mi) wide, of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> along the lower <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>. Cabinda borders the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Congo Republic">Congo Republic</a> to the north and north-northeast and the DRC to the east and south. The town of Cabinda is the chief population centre. </p>
      <p>According to a 1995 census, Cabinda had an estimated population of 600,000, approximately 400,000 of whom live in neighbouring countries. Population estimates are, however, highly unreliable. Consisting largely of tropical forest, Cabinda produces hardwoods, coffee, cocoa, crude rubber and palm oil. </p>
      <p>The product for which it is best known, however, is its oil, which has given it the nickname, "the Kuwait of Africa". Cabinda's petroleum production from its considerable offshore reserves now accounts for more than half of Angola's output.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Most of the oil along its coast was discovered under <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese rule</a> by the Cabinda Gulf Oil Company (CABGOC) from 1968 onwards. </p>
      <p>Ever since <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> handed over sovereignty of its former overseas province of Angola to the local independence groups (MPLA, UNITA and FNLA), the territory of Cabinda has been a focus of separatist guerrilla actions opposing the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Angola">Government of Angola</a> (which has employed its armed forces, the FAA—Forças Armadas Angolanas) and Cabindan separatists. The <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda</a>-<a href="/wiki/For%C3%A7as_Armadas_de_Cabinda" title="Forças Armadas de Cabinda">Armed Forces of Cabinda</a> (FLEC-FAC) announced a virtual Federal Republic of Cabinda under the Presidency of N'Zita Henriques Tiago. One of the characteristics of the Cabindan independence movement is its constant fragmentation, into smaller and smaller factions. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
