      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Angola" title="Politics of Angola">Politics of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Angola" title="Elections in Angola">Elections in Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Angola" title="List of political parties in Angola">List of political parties in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:National_Assembly_Building_(19898889148).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg/220px-National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg/330px-National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg/440px-National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:National_Assembly_Building_(19898889148).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Angola">National Assembly of Angola</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Angolan government is composed of three branches of government: executive, legislative and judicial. The executive branch of the government is composed of the President, the Vice-Presidents and the Council of Ministers. </p>
      <p>The legislative branch comprises a 220-seat <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislature, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Angola">National Assembly of Angola</a>, elected from both provincial and nationwide constituencies. For decades, political power has been concentrated in the presidency. </p>
      <p>After 38 years of rule, in 2017 President dos Santos stepped down from MPLA leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The leader of the winning party at the parliamentary elections in August 2017 would become the next president of Angola. The MPLA selected the former Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o" title="João Lourenço">João Lourenço</a> as Santos' chosen successor.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In what has been described as a political purge<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> to cement his power and reduce the influence of the Dos Santos family, Lourenço subsequently sacked the chief of the national police, Ambrósio de Lemos, and the head of the intelligence service, Apolinário José Pereira. Both are considered allies of former president Dos Santos.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> He also removed <a href="/wiki/Isabel_dos_Santos" title="Isabel dos Santos">Isabel Dos Santos</a>, daughter of the former president, as head of the country's state oil company Sonangol.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">Constitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o,_26_july_2018_(3)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o%2C_26_july_2018_%283%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o%2C_26_july_2018_%283%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o%2C_26_july_2018_%283%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o%2C_26_july_2018_%283%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o%2C_26_july_2018_%283%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o%2C_26_july_2018_%283%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1604" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o,_26_july_2018_(3)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o" title="João Lourenço">João Lourenço</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Angola" title="President of Angola">President of Angola</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of 2010</a> establishes the broad outlines of government structure and delineates the rights and duties of citizens. The legal system is based on Portuguese law and customary law but is weak and fragmented, and courts operate in only 12 of more than 140 municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> A Supreme Court serves as the appellate tribunal; a Constitutional Court does not hold the powers of <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review" title="Judicial review">judicial review</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-57">[57]</a></sup> Governors of the 18 provinces are appointed by the president. After the end of the civil war the regime came under pressure from within as well as from the international community to become more democratic and less authoritarian. Its reaction was to implement a number of changes without substantially changing its character.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">new constitution</a>, adopted in 2010, did away with presidential elections, introducing a system in which the president and the vice-president of the political party that wins the parliamentary elections automatically become president and vice-president. Directly or indirectly, the president controls all other organs of the state, so there is <i>de facto</i> no <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In the classifications used in constitutional law, this government falls under the category of <i>authoritarian regime.</i><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Armed_Forces" title="Angolan Armed Forces">Angolan Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Luanda_-_Angola_(6276460346)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Luanda_-_Angola_%286276460346%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Luanda_-_Angola_%286276460346%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Luanda_-_Angola_%286276460346%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Luanda_-_Angola_%286276460346%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Luanda_-_Angola_%286276460346%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Luanda_-_Angola_%286276460346%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2230" data-file-height="2063"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Luanda_-_Angola_(6276460346)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Armed_Forces" title="Angolan Armed Forces">Angolan Armed Forces</a> in <a href="/wiki/Full_dress_uniform" title="Full dress uniform">full dress uniform</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Angolan Armed Forces (AAF) are headed by a Chief of Staff who reports to the Minister of Defence. There are three divisions—the Army (Exército), Navy (Marinha de Guerra, MGA) and <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Force_of_Angola" title="National Air Force of Angola">National Air Force</a> (Força Aérea Nacional, FAN). Total manpower is 107,000; plus paramilitary forces of 10,000 (2015 est.).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Its equipment includes Russian-manufactured fighters, bombers and transport planes. There are also Brazilian-made <a href="/wiki/EMB-312_Tucano" class="mw-redirect" title="EMB-312 Tucano">EMB-312 Tucanos</a> for training, Czech-made L-39s for training and bombing, and a variety of western-made aircraft such as the C-212\Aviocar, Sud Aviation Alouette III, etc. A small number of AAF personnel are stationed in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (Kinshasa) and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> (Brazzaville). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police">Police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Angola_transito_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Angola_transito_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Angola_transito_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Angola_transito_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Angola_transito_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Angola_transito_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="438" data-file-height="263"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Angola_transito_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Angolan National Police officers.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The National Police departments are Public Order, Criminal Investigation, Traffic and Transport, Investigation and Inspection of Economic Activities, Taxation and Frontier Supervision, Riot Police and the Rapid Intervention Police. The National Police are in the process of standing up an air wing,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> to provide helicopter support for operations. The National Police are developing their criminal investigation and forensic capabilities. The force has an estimated 6,000 patrol officers, 2,500 taxation and frontier supervision officers, 182 criminal investigators and 100 financial crimes detectives and around 90 economic activity inspectors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The National Police have implemented a modernisation and development plan to increase the capabilities and efficiency of the total force. In addition to administrative reorganisation, modernisation projects include procurement of new vehicles, aircraft and equipment, construction of new police stations and forensic laboratories, restructured training programmes and the replacement of <a href="/wiki/AKM_rifle" class="mw-redirect" title="AKM rifle">AKM rifles</a> with 9&nbsp;mm <a href="/wiki/Uzi" title="Uzi">Uzis</a> for officers in urban areas. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice">Justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>A Supreme Court serves as a court of appeal. The Constitutional Court is the supreme body of the constitutional jurisdiction, established with the approval of Law no. 2/08, of 17 June – Organic Law of the Constitutional Court and Law n. 3/08, of 17 June – Organic Law of the Constitutional Process. The legal system is based on Portuguese and customary laws, but it is weak and fragmented. There are only 12 courts in more than 140 counties in the country. Its first task was the validation of the candidacies of the political parties to the legislative elections of 5 September 2008. Thus, on 25 June 2008, the Constitutional Court was institutionalized and its Judicial Counselors assumed the position before the President of the Republic. Currently, seven advisory judges are present, four men and three women. </p>
      <p>In 2014, a new penal code took effect in Angola. The classification of <a href="/wiki/Money-laundering" class="mw-redirect" title="Money-laundering">money-laundering</a> as a crime is one of the novelties in the new legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Angola" title="Foreign relations of Angola">Foreign relations of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Angola" title="List of diplomatic missions of Angola">List of diplomatic missions of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_(48578221376)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_%2848578221376%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_%2848578221376%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_%2848578221376%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_%2848578221376%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_%2848578221376%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_%2848578221376%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1070" data-file-height="1148"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Meets_With_Angolan_Foreign_Minister_Augusto_(48578221376)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Minister_of_External_Relations_(Angola)" title="Minister of External Relations (Angola)">Foreign Minister of Angola</a> <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Domingos_Augusto" title="Manuel Domingos Augusto">Manuel Domingos Augusto</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG/250px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG" decoding="async" width="250" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG/375px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG/500px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="625"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Diplomatic missions of Angola.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Angola is a founding member state of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), also known as the Lusophone Commonwealth, an international organization and political association of <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations across four continents, where <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is an official language. </p>
      <p>On 16 October 2014, Angola was elected for the second time a non-permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, with 190 favorable votes out of a total of 193. The term of office began on 1 January 2015 and expired on 31 December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since January 2014, the Republic of Angola has been chairing the International Conference for the Great Lakes Region (CIRGL). [80] In 2015, CIRGL Executive Secretary Ntumba Luaba said that Angola is the example to be followed by the members of the organization, due to the significant progress made during the 12 years of peace, namely in terms of socio-economic stability and political- military.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Angola" title="Human rights in Angola">Human rights in Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Angola" title="LGBT rights in Angola">LGBT rights in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Angola is classified as 'not free' by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> 2014 report.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-65">[65]</a></sup> The report noted that the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_legislative_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Angolan legislative election, 2012">August 2012 parliamentary elections</a>, in which the ruling <a href="/wiki/Popular_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola">Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> won more than 70% of the vote, suffered from serious flaws, including outdated and inaccurate voter rolls.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-65">[65]</a></sup> Voter turnout dropped from 80% in 2008 to 60%.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A 2012 report by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="United States State Department">U.S. Department of State</a> said, "The three most important <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> abuses [in 2012] were official corruption and impunity; limits on the freedoms of assembly, association, speech, and press; and cruel and excessive punishment, including reported cases of torture and beatings as well as unlawful killings by police and other security personnel."<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Angola ranked forty-two of forty-eight sub-Saharan African states on the 2007 Index of African Governance list and scored poorly on the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8</span></sup> It was ranked 39 out of 52 <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan African</a> countries, scoring particularly badly in the areas of participation and human rights, sustainable economic opportunity and human development. The Ibrahim Index uses a number of variables to compile its list which reflects the state of governance in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexual</a> acts were decriminalized in Angola, and the government also prohibited discrimination based on sexual orientation. The vote was overwhelming: 155 for, 1 against, 7 abstaining.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Angola" title="Economy of Angola">Economy of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_(8222830395).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_%288222830395%29.jpg/220px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_%288222830395%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_%288222830395%29.jpg/330px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_%288222830395%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_%288222830395%29.jpg/440px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_%288222830395%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_2_(8222830395).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porto_de_Luanda" class="extiw" title="pt:Porto de Luanda">Port of Luanda</a> is one of the busiest ports in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-africanbusinesscentral.com_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanbusinesscentral.com-70">[70]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1208" data-file-height="1610"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sonangol_building_-_Luanda_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Sonangol" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonangol">Sonangol</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_%28cropped%29.JPG/440px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2639" data-file-height="1544"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_03_(cropped).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>High rises in downtown <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Angola has diamonds, oil, gold, copper and a rich wildlife (dramatically impoverished during the civil war), forest and fossil fuels. Since independence, oil and diamonds have been the most important economic resource. <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">Smallholder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantation</a> agriculture dramatically dropped in the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>, but began to recover after 2002. </p>
      <p>Angola's economy has in recent years moved on from the disarray caused by a quarter-century of <a href="/wiki/Angolan_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Angolan civil war">Angolan civil war</a> to become the fastest-growing economy in Africa and one of the fastest-growing in the world, with an average <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> growth of 20% between 2005 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In the period 2001–10, Angola had the world's highest <a href="/wiki/Annual_average_GDP_growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Annual average GDP growth">annual average GDP growth</a>, at 11.1%. </p>
      <p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Exim_Bank_of_China" title="Exim Bank of China">Exim Bank of China</a> approved a $2&nbsp;billion <a href="/wiki/Line_of_credit" title="Line of credit">line of credit</a> to Angola, to be used for rebuilding Angola's <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>, and to limit the influence of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> there.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>China is Angola's biggest trade partner and <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> destination as well as the fourth-largest source of <a href="/wiki/Import" title="Import">imports</a>. Bilateral trade reached $27.67&nbsp;billion in 2011, up 11.5% year-on-year. China's imports, mainly <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> and diamonds, increased 9.1% to $24.89&nbsp;billion while China's exports to Angola, including mechanical and electrical products, machinery parts and construction materials, surged 38.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The oil <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">glut</a> led to a local <a href="/wiki/Price" title="Price">price</a> for unleaded gasoline of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>0.37 a gallon.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Angolan economy grew 18% in 2005, 26% in 2006 and 17.6% in 2007. Due to the global <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> the economy contracted an estimated −0.3% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-57">[57]</a></sup> The security brought about by the 2002 peace settlement has allowed the resettlement of 4&nbsp;million displaced persons and a resulting large-scale increases in agriculture production. Angola's economy is expected to grow by 3.9 percent in 2014 said the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), robust growth in the non-oil economy, mainly driven by a very good performance in the agricultural sector, is expected to offset a temporary drop in oil production.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/220px-Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/330px-Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/440px-Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Angola" title="National Bank of Angola">National Bank of Angola</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Angola's financial system is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Angola" title="National Bank of Angola">National Bank of Angola</a> and managed by governor <a href="https://no.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jose_de_Lima_Massano" class="extiw" title="no:Jose de Lima Massano">Jose de Lima Massano</a>. According to a study on the banking sector, carried out by <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, the monetary policy led by <a href="/wiki/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Banco Nacional de Angola">Banco Nacional de Angola</a> (BNA), the Angolan national bank, allowed a decrease in the inflation rate put at 7.96% in December 2013, which contributed to the sector's growth trend.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Estimates released by Angola's central bank, said country's economy should grow at an annual average rate of 5 percent over the next four years, boosted by the increasing participation of the private sector.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the country's economy has grown significantly since Angola achieved political stability in 2002, mainly due to fast-rising earnings in the oil sector, Angola faces huge social and economic problems. These are in part a result of almost continual armed conflict from 1961 on, although the highest level of destruction and socio-economic damage took place after the 1975 independence, during the long years of <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war</a>. However, high <a href="/wiki/Poverty_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Poverty rate">poverty rates</a> and blatant <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">social inequality</a> chiefly stem from persistent <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a>, "neo-patrimonial" practices at all levels of the political, administrative, military and economic structures, and of <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Angola" title="Corruption in Angola">a pervasive corruption</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> The main beneficiaries are political, administrative, economic and military power holders, who have accumulated (and continue to accumulate) enormous wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1468" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_Financeira_de_Luanda_2_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Luanda Financial City.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>"Secondary beneficiaries" are the middle strata which are about to become <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social classes</a>. However, almost half the population has to be considered poor, with dramatic differences between the countryside and the cities (where by now slightly more than 50% of the people live). </p>
      <p>A study carried out in 2008 by the Angolan Instituto Nacional de Estatística found that in rural areas roughly 58% must be classified as "poor" according to UN norms, but in the urban areas only 19%, and an overall rate of 37%.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In cities, a majority of families, well beyond those officially classified as poor, must adopt a variety of survival strategies.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In urban areas social inequality is most evident and it is extreme in Luanda.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> Angola constantly ranks in the bottom group.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG/220px-Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG/330px-Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG/440px-Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_in_Lobito.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Angola" title="Tourism in Angola">Tourism in Angola</a> has grown with the country's economy and stability.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In January 2020, a leak of government documents known as the <i>Luanda Leaks</i> showed that U.S. consulting companies such as <a href="/wiki/Boston_Consulting_Group" title="Boston Consulting Group">Boston Consulting Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/McKinsey_%26_Company" title="McKinsey &amp; Company">McKinsey &amp; Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> had helped members of the family of former President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos" title="José Eduardo dos Santos">José Eduardo dos Santos</a> (especially his daughter <a href="/wiki/Isabel_dos_Santos" title="Isabel dos Santos">Isabel dos Santos</a>) corruptly run Sonangol for their own personal profit, helping them use the company's revenues to fund vanity projects in France and Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The enormous differences between the regions pose a serious structural problem for the Angolan economy, illustrated by the fact that about one third of economic activities are concentrated in Luanda and neighbouring Bengo province, while several areas of the interior suffer economic stagnation and even regression.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One of the economic consequences of the social and regional disparities is a sharp increase in Angolan private investments abroad. The small fringe of Angolan society where most of the asset accumulation takes place seeks to spread its assets, for reasons of security and profit. For the time being, the biggest share of these investments is concentrated in Portugal where the <a href="/wiki/Angolans_in_Portugal" title="Angolans in Portugal">Angolan presence</a> (including the family of the state president) in banks as well as in the domains of energy, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Angola" title="Telecommunications in Angola">telecommunications</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">mass media</a> has become notable, as has the acquisition of vineyards and orchards as well as of touristic enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG/220px-Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG/330px-Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG/440px-Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rua_Kwame_Nkrumah_Luanda_05.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Corporate headquarters in Luanda
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Angola has upgraded critical infrastructure, an investment made possible by funds from the nation's development of oil resources.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> According to a report, just slightly more than ten years after the end of the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war</a> Angola's standard of living has overall greatly improved. Life expectancy, which was just 46 years in 2002, reached 51 in 2011. Mortality rates for children fell from 25 percent in 2001 to 19 percent in 2010 and the number of students enrolled in primary school has tripled since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> However, at the same time the social and economic inequality that has characterised the country for so long has not diminished, but on the contrary deepened in all respects. </p>
      <p>With a stock of assets corresponding to 70&nbsp;billion Kz (US$6.8&nbsp;billion), Angola is now the third-largest financial market in sub-Saharan Africa, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and South Africa. According to the Angolan Minister of Economy, Abraão Gourgel, the financial market of the country grew modestly from 2002 and now lies in third place at the level of sub-Saharan Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 December 2014, the Capital Market in Angola started. <a href="/wiki/Angola_Stock_Exchange_and_Derivatives" title="Angola Stock Exchange and Derivatives">BODIVA</a> (Angola Stock Exchange and Derivatives, in English) received the secondary public debt market, and it is expected to start the corporate debt market by 2015, but the stock market should be a reality only in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination,_Ilha_de_Luanda_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda_%28cropped%29.JPG/440px-Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1026" data-file-height="879"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination,_Ilha_de_Luanda_(cropped).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">offshore oil drilling platform</a> off the coast of central Angola
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> reported in 2008 that diamonds and oil make up 60% of Angola's economy, almost all of the country's <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a> and all of its dominant <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">exports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Growth is almost entirely driven by rising <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">oil production</a> which surpassed 1.4 million barrels per day (220,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d) in late 2005 and was expected to grow to 2 million barrels per day (320,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d) by 2007. Control of the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil industry</a> is consolidated in <a href="/wiki/Sonangol_Group" title="Sonangol Group">Sonangol Group</a>, a conglomerate owned by the Angolan government. In December 2006, Angola was admitted as a member of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">the Heritage Foundation</a>, a conservative American <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a>, oil production from Angola has increased so significantly that Angola now is China's biggest supplier of oil.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> "China has extended three multibillion dollar lines of credit to the Angolan government; two loans of $2 billion from China Exim Bank, one in 2004, the second in 2007, as well as one loan in 2005 of $2.9 billion from <a href="/wiki/China_International_Fund" title="China International Fund">China International Fund</a> Ltd."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Growing oil revenues also created opportunities for <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Angola" title="Corruption in Angola">corruption</a>: according to a recent <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> report, 32&nbsp;billion US dollars disappeared from government accounts in 2007–2010.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Sonangol" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonangol">Sonangol</a>, the state-run oil company, controls 51% of Cabinda's oil. Due to this market control the company ends up determining the profit received by the government and the taxes it pays. The council of foreign affairs states that the World Bank mentioned that Sonangol " is a taxpayer, it carries out quasi-fiscal activities, it invests public funds, and, as concessionaire, it is a sector regulator. This multifarious work programme creates conflicts of interest and characterises a complex relationship between Sonangol and the government that weakens the formal budgetary process and creates uncertainty as regards the actual fiscal stance of the state."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2002 Angola demanded compensation for <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil spills</a> allegedly caused by <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a>, the first time it had fined a multinational corporation operating in its waters.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Operations in its <a href="/wiki/List_of_diamond_mines" title="List of diamond mines">diamond mines</a> include partnerships between state-run <a href="/wiki/Endiama" title="Endiama">Endiama</a> and mining companies such as <a href="/wiki/ALROSA" class="mw-redirect" title="ALROSA">ALROSA</a> which operate in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Angola is higher than world average. In 2016, Angola had 1.9 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-100">[100]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, slightly more than world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In 2016 Angola used 1.01 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use about half as much biocapacity as Angola contains. As a result, Angola is running a biocapacity reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg/220px-HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg/330px-HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg/440px-HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="448" data-file-height="336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HPP_%22CAPANDA%22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Capanda_Dam" title="Capanda Dam">Capanda Dam</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Cuanza_River" title="Cuanza River">Cuanza</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Angola" title="Agriculture in Angola">Agriculture in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Agriculture and forestry is an area of potential opportunity for the country. The African Economic Outlook organization states that "Angola requires 4.5 million tonnes a year of grain but grows only about 55% of the <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> it needs, 20% of the <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and just 5% of its required <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition, the World Bank estimates that "less than 3 percent of Angola's abundant fertile land is cultivated and the economic potential of the forestry sector remains largely unexploited" .<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before independence in 1975, <a href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angola (Portugal)">Angola</a> was a breadbasket of southern Africa and a major exporter of <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, coffee and <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">three decades of civil war</a> (1975–2002) destroyed fertile countryside, left it littered with <a href="/wiki/Landmine" class="mw-redirect" title="Landmine">landmines</a> and drove millions into the cities. </p>
      <p>The country now depends on expensive food imports, mainly from South Africa and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, while more than 90% of farming is done at the family and subsistence level. Thousands of Angolan small-scale farmers are trapped in poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Angola" title="Transport in Angola">Transport in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png/220px-TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png/330px-TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png/440px-TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png 2x" data-file-width="1270" data-file-height="928"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TAAG_Angola_Airlines_Boeing_737-200Adv_D2-TBD_CDG_July_1986.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/TAAG_Angola_Airlines" title="TAAG Angola Airlines">TAAG Angola Airlines</a> is the country's state-owned <a href="/wiki/National_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="National carrier">national carrier</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transport in Angola consists of: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Three separate <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Angola" title="Rail transport in Angola">railway systems</a> totalling 2,761&nbsp;km (1,716&nbsp;mi)</li> 
       <li>76,626&nbsp;km (47,613&nbsp;mi) of highway of which 19,156&nbsp;km (11,903&nbsp;mi) is paved</li> 
       <li>1,295 navigable inland waterways</li> 
       <li>Eight major <a href="/wiki/Sea_port" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea port">sea ports</a></li> 
       <li>243 <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Angola" title="List of airports in Angola">airports</a>, of which 32 are paved.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Angola centers its port trade in five main ports: <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Namibe" title="Port of Namibe">Namibe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Lobito" title="Port of Lobito">Lobito</a>, Soyo, Cabinda and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Luanda" title="Port of Luanda">Luanda</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Luanda" title="Port of Luanda">port of Luanda</a> is the largest of the five, as well as being one of the busiest on the African continent.<sup id="cite_ref-africanbusinesscentral.com_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanbusinesscentral.com-70">[70]</a></sup> Major expansion of this port is also taking place.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Catumbela_River_Bridge_(19478241049).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Catumbela_River_Bridge_%2819478241049%29.jpg/220px-Catumbela_River_Bridge_%2819478241049%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Catumbela_River_Bridge_%2819478241049%29.jpg/330px-Catumbela_River_Bridge_%2819478241049%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Catumbela_River_Bridge_%2819478241049%29.jpg/440px-Catumbela_River_Bridge_%2819478241049%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Catumbela_River_Bridge_(19478241049).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Catumbela" title="Catumbela">Catumbela</a> Bridge in <a href="/wiki/Benguela_Province" title="Benguela Province">Benguela</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Travel on highways outside of towns and cities in Angola (and in some cases within) is often not best advised for those without four-by-four vehicles. While a reasonable road infrastructure has existed within Angola, time and the war have taken their toll on the road surfaces, leaving many severely potholed, littered with broken asphalt. In many areas drivers have established alternate tracks to avoid the worst parts of the surface, although careful attention must be paid to the presence or absence of landmine warning markers by the side of the road. The Angolan government has contracted the restoration of many of the country's roads. The road between Lubango and Namibe, for example, was completed recently with funding from the European Union, and is comparable to many European main routes. Completing the road infrastructure is likely to take some decades, but substantial efforts are already being made.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="811" data-file-height="453"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Porto_do_Lobito_-_Angola_2015_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lobito" title="Lobito">Lobito</a> hosts a major seaport.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_(cropped).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_%28cropped%29.JPG/440px-Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="1992"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Marginal_Avenida_4_de_Fevreiro_Luanda_March_2013_13_(cropped).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>'s construction boom is financed largely by oil and diamonds.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunications</a> industry is considered one of the main strategic sectors in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2014, the building of an <a href="/wiki/Optic_fiber" class="mw-redirect" title="Optic fiber">optic fiber</a> underwater cable was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> This project aims to turn Angola into a continental hub, thus improving Internet connections both nationally and internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 11 March 2015, the First Angolan Forum of Telecommunications and Information Technology was held in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> under the motto "The challenges of telecommunications in the current context of Angola",<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> to promote debate on topical issues on <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> in Angola and worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> A study of this sector, presented at the forum, said Angola had the first telecommunications operator in Africa to test LTE – with speeds up to 400 Mbit/s – and mobile penetration of about 75%; there are about 3.5 million <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> in the Angolan market; There are about 25,000 kilometres (16,000 miles) of optical fibre installed in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first Angolan <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angosat_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Angosat 1">AngoSat-1</a>, was launched into orbit on 26 December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> It was launched from the <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">Baikonur space center</a> in Kazakhstan on board a <a href="/wiki/Zenit-3F" title="Zenit-3F">Zenit 3F</a> rocket. The satellite was built by Russia's <a href="/wiki/RSC_Energia" class="mw-redirect" title="RSC Energia">RSC Energia</a>, a subsidiary of the state-run space industry player <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">Roscosmos</a>. The satellite payload was supplied by <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_%26_Space" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus Defence &amp; Space">Airbus Defence &amp; Space</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Due to an on-board power failure during solar panel deployment, on 27 December, RSC Energia revealed that they lost communications contact with the satellite. Although, subsequent attempts to restore communications with the satellite were successful, the satellite eventually stopped sending data and RSC Energia confirmed that AngoSat-1 was inoperable. The launch of AngoSat-1 was aimed at ensuring telecommunications throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> According to Aristides Safeca, Secretary of State for Telecommunications, the satellite was aimed at providing telecommunications services, TV, internet and <a href="/wiki/E-government" title="E-government">e-government</a> and was expected to remain in orbit "at best" for 18 years.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> A replacement satellite named AngoSat-2 is in the works and is expected to be in service by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The management of the <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a> '.ao' passed from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> to Angola in 2015, following new legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> A joint decree of minister of Telecommunications and Information Technologies José Carvalho da Rocha and the minister of Science and Technology, Maria Cândida Pereira Teixeira, states that "under the massification" of that Angolan domain, "conditions are created for the transfer of the domain root '.ao' of Portugal to Angola".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Angola" title="Demographics of Angola">Demographics of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png/220px-Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png/330px-Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png/440px-Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="727"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population Pyramid of Angola.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <p>Angola has a population of 24,383,301 inhabitants according to the preliminary results of its 2014 census, the first one conducted or carried out since 15 December 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-INE_Angola_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INE_Angola-3">[3]</a></sup> It is composed of <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> (language <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>) 37%, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mbundu_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Mbundu people">Ambundu</a> (language <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a>) 23%, <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a> 13%, and 32% other ethnic groups (including the <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_people" title="Chokwe people">Chokwe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ganguela" title="Ganguela">Ganguela</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Xindonga" title="Xindonga">Xindonga</a>) as well as about 2% <i><a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mestiço">mestiços</a></i> (mixed European and African), 1.6% Chinese and 1% European.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-57">[57]</a></sup> The Ambundu and Ovimbundu ethnic groups combined form a majority of the population, at 62%.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The population is forecast to grow to over 60 million people to 2050, 2.7 times the 2014 population.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> However, on 23 March 2016, official data revealed by Angola's National Statistic Institute – Instituto Nacional de Estatística (INE), states that Angola has a population of 25,789,024 inhabitants. </p>
      <p>It is estimated that Angola was host to 12,100 refugees and 2,900 asylum seekers by the end of 2007. 11,400 of those refugees were originally from the Democratic Republic of Congo, who arrived in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were an estimated 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> migrant workers,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> at least 220,000 <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angolans" title="Portuguese Angolans">Portuguese</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Observatório_da_Emigração_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observatório_da_Emigração-126">[126]</a></sup> and about 259,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Angola" title="Chinese people in Angola">Chinese living in Angola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> 1 million Angolans are <a href="/wiki/Mixed_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed race">mixed race</a> (black and white). </p>
      <p>Since 2003, more than 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> migrants have been expelled from Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Prior to independence in 1975, Angola had a community of approximately 350,000 Portuguese,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> but the vast majority left after independence and the ensuing civil war. However, Angola has recovered its Portuguese minority in recent years; currently, there are about 200,000 registered with the consulates, and increasing due to the debt crisis in Portugal and the relative prosperity in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The Chinese population stands at 258,920, mostly composed of temporary migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Also, there is a small <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> community of about 5,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of Angola is 5.54 children born per woman (2012 estimates), the 11th highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <p>The languages in Angola are those originally spoken by the different ethnic groups and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, introduced during the Portuguese colonial era. The most widely spoken indigenous languages are <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kikongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Kikongo">Kikongo</a>, in that order. Portuguese is the official language of the country. </p>
      <p>Although the exact numbers of those fluent in Portuguese or who speak Portuguese as a first language are unknown, a 2012 study mentions that Portuguese is the first language of 39% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 2014, a census carried out by the Instituto Nacional de Estatística in Angola mentions that 71.15% of the nearly 25.8 million inhabitants of Angola (meaning around 18.3 million people) use Portuguese as a first or second language.<sup id="cite_ref-Angola:_português_é_falado_por_71,15%_de_angolanos_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angola:_português_é_falado_por_71,15%_de_angolanos-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2014 census, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is spoken by 71.1% of Angolans, <a href="/wiki/Umbundu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Umbundu language">Umbundu</a> by 23%, <a href="/wiki/Kikongo_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kikongo language">Kikongo</a> by 8.2%, <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> by 7.8%, <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_language" title="Chokwe language">Chokwe</a> by 6.5%, <a href="/wiki/Nyaneka_language" title="Nyaneka language">Nyaneka</a> by 3.4%, <a href="/wiki/Ngangela_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ngangela language">Ngangela</a> by 3.1%, <a href="/wiki/Fiote_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiote language">Fiote</a> by 2.4%, <a href="/wiki/Kwanyama_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwanyama language">Kwanyama</a> by 2.3%, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Muhumbi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Muhumbi language (page does not exist)">Muhumbi</a> by 2.1%, <a href="/wiki/Luvale_language" title="Luvale language">Luvale</a> by 1%, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Angola" title="Languages of Angola">other languages</a> by 4.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-Censo2014_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Censo2014-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
