      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_(19929834976).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_%2819929834976%29.jpg/220px-Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_%2819929834976%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_%2819929834976%29.jpg/330px-Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_%2819929834976%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_%2819929834976%29.jpg/440px-Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_%2819929834976%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Igreja_de_Nossa_Senhora_dos_Rem%C3%A9dios_(19929834976).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Luanda_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Luanda Cathedral">Luanda Cathedral</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are about 1,000 religious communities, mostly Christian, in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> While reliable statistics are nonexistent, estimates have it that more than half of the population are Catholics, while about a quarter adhere to the Protestant churches introduced during the colonial period: the <a href="/wiki/Congregationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregationalist">Congregationalists</a> mainly among the <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> of the Central Highlands and the coastal region to its west, the <a href="/wiki/Methodists" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> concentrating on the <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> speaking strip from Luanda to Malanje, the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> almost exclusively among the <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a> of the north-west (now present in Luanda as well) and dispersed <a href="/wiki/Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Adventists">Adventists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Luanda and region there subsists a nucleus of the "<a href="/wiki/Syncretic" class="mw-redirect" title="Syncretic">syncretic</a>" <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tocoists&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tocoists (page does not exist)">Tocoists</a> and in the north-west a sprinkling of <a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a> can be found, spreading from the Congo/Zaïre. Since independence, hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> and similar communities have sprung up in the cities, where by now about 50% of the population is living; several of these communities/churches are of Brazilian origin. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%282%29.jpg/220px-Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%282%29.jpg/330px-Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%282%29.jpg/440px-Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2997" data-file-height="2247"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Igreja_Matriz_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Catholic church of <a href="/wiki/Uaco_Cungo" title="Uaco Cungo">Uaco Cungo</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a> estimates the Muslim population at 80,000–90,000, less than 1% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola" title="Islam in Angola">Islamic Community of Angola</a> puts the figure closer to 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Muslims consist largely of migrants from West Africa and the Middle East (especially <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>), although some are local converts.<sup id="cite_ref-customs_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-customs-143">[143]</a></sup> The Angolan government does not <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola#Legal_status" title="Islam in Angola">legally recognize</a> any Muslim organizations and often shuts down mosques or prevents their construction.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In a study assessing nations' levels of religious regulation and persecution with scores ranging from 0 to 10 where 0 represented low levels of regulation or persecution, Angola was scored 0.8 on Government Regulation of Religion, 4.0 on Social Regulation of Religion, 0 on Government Favoritism of Religion and 0 on Religious Persecution.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Foreign <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> were very active prior to independence in 1975, although since the beginning of the anti-colonial fight in 1961 the Portuguese colonial authorities expelled a series of Protestant missionaries and closed mission stations based on the belief that the missionaries were inciting pro-independence sentiments. Missionaries have been able to return to the country since the early 1990s, although security conditions due to the civil war have prevented them until 2002 from restoring many of their former inland mission stations.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Catholic Church and some major Protestant denominations mostly keep to themselves in contrast to the "New Churches" which actively proselytize. Catholics, as well as some major Protestant denominations, provide help for the poor in the form of crop seeds, farm animals, medical care and education.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">9</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Cu%C3%ADto" title="Cuíto">Cuíto</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Bi%C3%A9_Province" title="Bié Province">Bié</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">355,423 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/U%C3%ADge" title="Uíge">Uíge</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/U%C3%ADge_Province" title="Uíge Province">Uíge</a></td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Angola" title="Health in Angola">Health in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="323"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maternidade_Lucr%C3%A9cia_Pa%C3%ADm_-_panoramio_-_Rog%C3%A9rio_Melo_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lucrécia Paím Maternity Hospital.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Epidemics of <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabies" title="Rabies">rabies</a> and African <a href="/wiki/Hemorrhagic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hemorrhagic">hemorrhagic</a> fevers like <a href="/wiki/Marburg_virus" title="Marburg virus">Marburg hemorrhagic fever</a>, are common diseases in several parts of the country. Many regions in this country have high incidence rates of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and high <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in Africa">HIV prevalence</a> rates. <a href="/wiki/Dengue" class="mw-redirect" title="Dengue">Dengue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filariasis" title="Filariasis">filariasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leishmaniasis" title="Leishmaniasis">leishmaniasis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">onchocerciasis</a> (river blindness) are other diseases carried by insects that also occur in the region. Angola has one of the highest <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rates</a> in the world and one of the world's lowest <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancies" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancies">life expectancies</a>. A 2007 survey concluded that low and deficient <a href="/wiki/Niacin" title="Niacin">niacin</a> status was common in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> is currently conducting several surveys in Angola on malaria, domestic violence and more.<sup id="cite_ref-Angola_Surveys_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angola_Surveys-151">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2014, the Angolan Institute for Cancer Control (IACC) was created by presidential decree, and it will integrate the National Health Service in Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The purpose of this new centre is to ensure health and medical care in <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">oncology</a>, policy implementation, programmes and plans for prevention and specialised treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> This cancer institute will be assumed as a reference institution in the central and southern regions of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, Angola launched a national campaign of <a href="/wiki/Vaccination" title="Vaccination">vaccination</a> against <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, extended to every child under ten years old and aiming to go to all 18 provinces in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> The measure is part of the Strategic Plan for the Elimination of Measles 2014–2020 created by the Angolan Ministry of Health which includes strengthening routine immunisation, a proper dealing with measles cases, national campaigns, introducing a second dose of vaccination in the national routine vaccination calendar and active epidemiological surveillance for measles. This campaign took place together with the vaccination against <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_A" title="Vitamin A">vitamin A</a> supplementation.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/2016_Angola_and_DR_Congo_yellow_fever_outbreak" title="2016 Angola and DR Congo yellow fever outbreak">yellow fever</a> outbreak, the worst in the country in three decades<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> began in December 2015. By August 2016, when the outbreak began to subside, nearly 4,000 people were suspected of being infected. As many as 369 may have died. The outbreak began in the capital, Luanda, and spread to at least 16 of the 18 provinces. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Angola" title="Education in Angola">Education in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:New_campus_(6177681401)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/New_campus_%286177681401%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-New_campus_%286177681401%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/New_campus_%286177681401%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-New_campus_%286177681401%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/New_campus_%286177681401%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-New_campus_%286177681401%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3251" data-file-height="2331"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:New_campus_(6177681401)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto_University" title="Agostinho Neto University">Agostinho Neto University</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Although by law education in Angola is compulsory and free for eight years, the government reports that a percentage of pupils are not attending due to a lack of school buildings and teachers.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> Pupils are often responsible for paying additional school-related expenses, including fees for books and supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1999, the gross primary enrollment rate was 74 percent and in 1998, the most recent year for which data are available, the net primary enrollment rate was 61 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> Gross and net enrollment ratios are based on the number of pupils formally registered in primary school and therefore do not necessarily reflect actual school attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> There continue to be significant disparities in enrollment between rural and urban areas. In 1995, 71.2 percent of children ages 7 to 14 years were attending school.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> It is reported that higher percentages of boys attend school than girls.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a> (1975–2002), nearly half of all schools were reportedly looted and destroyed, leading to current problems with overcrowding.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Waku_Kungo,_Angola_-_panoramio_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Waku_Kungo%2C_Angola_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Waku_Kungo%2C_Angola_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Waku_Kungo%2C_Angola_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Waku_Kungo%2C_Angola_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Waku_Kungo%2C_Angola_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Waku_Kungo%2C_Angola_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="2487"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Waku_Kungo,_Angola_-_panoramio_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A primary school in <a href="/wiki/Cuanza_Sul_Province" title="Cuanza Sul Province">Province of Cuanza Sul</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Ministry of Education recruited 20,000 new teachers in 2005 and continued to implement teacher trainings.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> Teachers tend to be underpaid, inadequately trained and overworked (sometimes teaching two or three shifts a day).<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> Some teachers may reportedly demand payment or bribes directly from their pupils.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> Other factors, such as the presence of landmines, lack of resources and identity papers, and poor health prevent children from regularly attending school.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> Although budgetary allocations for education were increased in 2004, the education system in Angola continues to be extremely under-funded.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_158-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to estimates by the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UNESCO Institute for Statistics</a>, the adult literacy rate in 2011 was 70.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-unescolit_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-159">[159]</a></sup> By 2015, this had increased to 71.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> 82.9% of males and 54.2% of women are literate as of 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Since independence from Portugal in 1975, a number of Angolan students continued to be admitted every year at high schools, <a href="/wiki/Politechnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Politechnic">polytechnical</a> institutes and universities in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> through bilateral agreements; in general, these students belong to the elites. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda,_Angola_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="788" data-file-height="463"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda,_Angola_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magist%C3%A9rio_Mutu-ya-Kevela" class="extiw" title="pt:Magistério Mutu-ya-Kevela">Mutu-ya Kevela Prep. School</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In September 2014, the Angolan Ministry of Education announced an investment of 16 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euros</a> in the computerisation of over 300 classrooms across the country. The project also includes training teachers at a national level, "as a way to introduce and use new information technologies in primary schools, thus reflecting an improvement in the quality of teaching".<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2010, the Angolan government started building the Angolan Media Libraries Network, distributed throughout several provinces in the country to facilitate the people's access to information and knowledge. Each site has a bibliographic archive, multimedia resources and computers with Internet access, as well as areas for reading, researching and socialising.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> The plan envisages the establishment of one media library in each Angolan province by 2017. The project also includes the implementation of several media libraries, in order to provide the several contents available in the fixed media libraries to the most isolated populations in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> At this time, the mobile media libraries are already operating in the provinces of Luanda, Malanje, Uíge, Cabinda and Lunda South. As for REMA, the provinces of Luanda, Benguela, Lubango and Soyo have currently working media libraries.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Angola" title="Culture of Angola">Culture of Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Angola" title="Music of Angola">Music of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angolan_cuisine" title="Angolan cuisine">Angolan cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_(19882325368).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_%2819882325368%29.jpg/170px-Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_%2819882325368%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_%2819882325368%29.jpg/255px-Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_%2819882325368%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_%2819882325368%29.jpg/340px-Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_%2819882325368%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Memorial_Antonio_Agostinho_Neto_(19882325368).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto" title="Agostinho Neto">Agostinho Neto</a> National Memorial in Luanda.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/170px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/255px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/340px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="2688"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Yombe_people" title="Yombe people">Yombe</a> sculpture.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Angolan culture has been heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese culture">Portuguese culture</a>, especially in terms of language and religion, and the culture of the indigenous ethnic groups of Angola, predominantly <a href="/wiki/Bantu_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu people">Bantu culture</a>. </p>
      <p>The diverse ethnic communities—the <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mbundu_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Mbundu people">Ambundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakongo" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_people" title="Chokwe people">Chokwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a> and other peoples—to varying degrees maintain their own cultural traits, traditions and languages, but in the cities, where slightly more than half of the population now lives, a mixed culture has been emerging since colonial times; in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, since its foundation in the 16th century. </p>
      <p>In this urban culture, the Portuguese heritage has become more and more dominant. African roots are evident in music and dance, and is moulding the way in which Portuguese is spoken. This process is well reflected in contemporary Angolan literature, especially in the works of <a href="/wiki/Angolan_literature" title="Angolan literature">Angolan authors</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2014, Angola resumed the National Festival of Angolan Culture after a 25-year break. The festival took place in all the provincial capitals and lasted for 20 days, with the theme ”Culture as a Factor of Peace and Development.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1972, one of Angola's first feature films, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Maldoror" title="Sarah Maldoror">Sarah Maldoror</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Co-production_(media)" title="Co-production (media)">internationally co-produced</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Sambizanga_(film)" title="Sambizanga (film)">Sambizanga</a></i>, was released at the <a href="/wiki/Carthage_Film_Festival" title="Carthage Film Festival">Carthage Film Festival</a> to critical acclaim, winning the <i>Tanit d'Or</i>, the festival's highest prize.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sports_in_Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sports in Angola (page does not exist)">Sports in Angola</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Museu_Nacional_de_Antropologia_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="614"></a>

      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_(19151153514)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_%2819151153514%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_%2819151153514%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="69" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_%2819151153514%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_%2819151153514%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_%2819151153514%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_%2819151153514%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="994" data-file-height="312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Est%C3%A1dio_Nacional_de_Ombaka_(19151153514)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The National Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> is the most popular sport in Angola. Its <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Angola national basketball team">national team</a> has won the <a href="/wiki/AfroBasket" title="AfroBasket">AfroBasket</a> 11 times and holds the record of most titles. As a top team in Africa, it is a regular competitor at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the Summer Olympics">Summer Olympic Games</a> and the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA World Cup">FIBA World Cup</a>. Angola is home to one of Africa's first competitive leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In football, Angola hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2010 Africa Cup of Nations">2010 Africa Cup of Nations</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_football_team" title="Angola national football team">Angola national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, their first appearance in the World Cup finals. They were eliminated after one defeat and two draws in the group stage. They won three <a href="/wiki/COSAFA_Cup" title="COSAFA Cup">COSAFA Cups</a> and finished runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/2011_African_Nations_Championship" title="2011 African Nations Championship">2011 African Nations Championship</a>. </p>
      <p>Angola has participated in the <a href="/wiki/World_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="World Women's Handball Championship">World Women's Handball Championship</a> for several years. The country has also appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Angola_at_the_Olympics" title="Angola at the Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> for seven years and both regularly competes in and once has hosted the <a href="/wiki/FIRS_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup">FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup</a>, where the best finish is sixth. Angola is also often believed to have historic roots in the <a href="/wiki/Martial_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Martial art">martial art</a> "<a href="/wiki/Capoeira_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Capoeira Angola">Capoeira Angola</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Batuque_(game)" title="Batuque (game)">Batuque</a>" which were practiced by <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Angola" title="Slavery in Angola">enslaved African Angolans</a> transported as part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
